<p><b><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the Olympics">Great Britain</a></b>, represented by the <a href="/wiki/British_Olympic_Association" title="British Olympic Association">British Olympic Association</a> (BOA), competed at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, from 13 to 29 August 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The British sent a wide-ranging delegation to the Games, continuing its ubiquitous presence in the Olympic games, the only country to have sent competitors to every summer and winter games since the birth of the modern Olympics in 1896. Great Britain's 264 athletes, 161 men and 103 women, competed in 22 disciplines throughout the two-week event. The team entered the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2004 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> behind the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Flag" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> carried by <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judoka</a> <a href="/wiki/Kate_Howey" title="Kate Howey">Kate Howey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khowey_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-khowey-1">[1]</a></sup> Double gold medal winner <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Holmes" title="Kelly Holmes">Kelly Holmes</a> carried the flag at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_Closing_Ceremony" title="2004 Summer Olympics Closing Ceremony">closing ceremony</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">Chronology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Chronology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The delegation started the Olympics slowly, the silver its divers won on 14 August being the first of only a few opening-week medals. Although a sprinkling of silver and bronze medals — including a pair in men's and women's k1 kayak slalom — enlivened the mid-week, Britain's first gold did not come until Friday the 20th (won by Chris Hoy in the 1 km track cycling time-trial).</p>
<p>Then, on 21 August ("Golden Saturday") Britain's contributions to the medal table became more significant. First Britain's traditional strength in rowing continued as the men's coxless four, stroked by <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Pinsent" title="Matthew Pinsent">Matthew Pinsent</a>, narrowly won gold, a defining moment since this was Pinsent's fourth gold medal in as many games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Sailor <a href="/wiki/Ben_Ainslie" title="Ben Ainslie">Ben Ainslie</a> wrapped up a successful few days of racing with a gold, as did the women's Yngling sailboats who were finally awarded the gold medal they had sewn up on Thursday. <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Wiggins" title="Bradley Wiggins">Bradley Wiggins</a> continued Britain's cycling success, winning gold in the 4 km pursuit. Young swimmer <a href="/wiki/David_Davies_(swimmer)" title="David Davies (swimmer)">David Davies</a>, coming third in the men's 1500 m freestyle, set a European record in the process and won Britain's second swimming medal of the games — a notable improvement over the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Sydney games</a> from which the swimmers had returned empty-handed. Also on Saturday, it was announced that, after an appeal, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Law" title="Leslie Law">Leslie Law</a> would be promoted from silver to gold in the three-day equestrian eventing (and his team from bronze to silver). As the games' aquatic-dominated first week shifted into a second week focused more on track and field events, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Sotherton" title="Kelly Sotherton">Kelly Sotherton</a> came third in the heptathlon.</p>
<p>Sunday 22 August brought another rowing medal. However, marathon favourite <a href="/wiki/Paula_Radcliffe" title="Paula Radcliffe">Paula Radcliffe</a> failed to cope with the heat of Athens and did not finish. The timing of the race with a late afternoon start, supposedly to appease US broadcasters, produced some controversy since summer marathons normally start early in the morning to avoid the heat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>23 August saw Britain's first gold medal of the track and field events, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Holmes" title="Kelly Holmes">Kelly Holmes</a> winning the women's 800 metres. This was Britain's first gold medal on the track since <a href="/wiki/Sally_Gunnell" title="Sally Gunnell">Sally Gunnell</a> won the 400 metre hurdles at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Barcelona games</a>.</p>
<p>By claiming bronze in the Madison cycling on 25 August, to add to his earlier individual gold and a silver from the team pursuit, <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Wiggins" title="Bradley Wiggins">Bradley Wiggins</a> became the first Briton for 40 years to claim three medals in one games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The evening of Saturday 28 August saw Britain's medal hunt centered on the Olympic Stadium. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Backley" title="Steve Backley">Steve Backley</a>, in his final <a href="/wiki/Javelin_throw" title="Javelin throw">javelin throw</a> competition, failed to win the gold he had been seeking since 1992, finishing fourth. Kelly Holmes achieved the middle-distance double, taking gold in the 1500 metres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The men's 4×100 metre relay team won a surprising victory, winning gold ahead of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="United States at the 2004 Summer Olympics">American</a> team. Earlier in the day, Ian Wynne had added to the medal haul, with a bronze medal in the K1 kayak class, competing despite an ankle injury picked up the day before.</p>
<p>The final day of the games, 29 August, saw <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amir_Khan_(British_boxer)" title="Amir Khan (British boxer)">Amir Khan</a> collect Britain's last medal of the event with a silver in <a href="/wiki/Boxing_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Boxing at the 2004 Summer Olympics">boxing</a>'s lightweight division.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_performance">Overall performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overall performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the final <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_medal_count" title="2004 Summer Olympics medal count">medal table</a>, Great Britain finished in 10th place overall. The BBC stated that this was "the best British performance in the modern era", and quantified this with further considerations: "GB won 37 in 1984, but that was a boycott-hit Games missing the Eastern Bloc countries. Take Los Angeles out of the picture, and this was Britain's best haul since 1924."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medallists">Medallists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Medallists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics_medal_table" title="2004 Summer Olympics medal table">2004 Summer Olympics medal table</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_2004_Summer_Olympics_medal_winners" title="List of 2004 Summer Olympics medal winners">List of 2004 Summer Olympics medal winners</a></div>
<p>Great Britain finished in tenth position in the final medal rankings, with 9 gold and 30 total medals.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiple_medallists">Multiple medallists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Multiple medallists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following Team GB competitors won multiple medals at the 2004 Olympic Games. <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Holmes" title="Kelly Holmes">Kelly Holmes</a> became the first British athlete since 1972 and the first British track and field athlete to win two gold medals at the same Summer Olympics.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archery">Archery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Archery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Archery_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Archery at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Archery at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>Four British archers (one man and three women) qualified each for the men's and women's individual archery, and a spot for the women's team.</p>

<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Archery_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_individual" title="Archery at the 2004 Summer Olympics – Men's individual">Men's individual</a></td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Athletics at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Athletics at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>British athletes have so far achieved qualifying standards in the following athletics events (up to a maximum of 3 athletes in each event at the 'A' Standard, and 1 at the 'B' Standard).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt><small>Key</small></dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><small><b>Note</b>–Ranks given for track events are within the athlete's heat only</small></li>
<li><small><b>Q</b> = Qualified for the next round</small></li>
<li><small><b>q</b> = Qualified for the next round as a fastest loser <i>or</i>, in field events, by position without achieving the qualifying target</small></li>
<li><small><b>NR</b> = National record</small></li>
<li><small>N/A = Round not applicable for the event</small></li>
<li><small>Bye = Athlete not required to compete in round</small></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing">Boxing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Boxing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boxing_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Boxing at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Boxing at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>Great Britain sent only one boxer to Athens, the 17-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amir_Khan_(British_boxer)" title="Amir Khan (British boxer)">Amir Khan</a>. Khan tore through his first four fights, including two that the referees had to stop prematurely. His loss in the final to the defending Olympic champion and three-time world champion gave Khan a 4-1 record and a silver medal; many hoped he would compete the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> but in the event he decided to turn professional later in 2004.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diving">Diving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Diving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Diving at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Diving at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>British divers qualified for eight individual spots at the 2004 Olympic Games. Three British synchronized diving teams qualified through the 2004 FINA Diving World Cup.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equestrian">Equestrian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Equestrian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Equestrian at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Equestrian at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>Because only three horse and rider pairs from each nation could advance beyond certain rounds in the individual events, five British pairs did not advance despite being placed sufficiently high. They received rankings below all pairs that did advance.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_pentathlon">Modern pentathlon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Modern pentathlon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swimming">Swimming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Swimming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Swimming_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Swimming at the 2004 Summer Olympics">Swimming at the 2004 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>British swimmers earned qualifying standards in the following events (up to a maximum of 2 swimmers in each event at the A-standard time, and 1 at the B-standard time): All British swimmers must qualify by finishing in the top two of the Olympic trials having gained the GB qualifying A standard set by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Swimming" title="British Swimming">British Swimming</a> in the relevant final (that time being the fastest time of the sixteenth fastest swimmer internationally in that event in 2003).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The main rights to Olympic coverage in the UK are held by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, under the <a href="/wiki/Ofcom_Code_on_Sports_and_Other_Listed_and_Designated_Events" title="Ofcom Code on Sports and Other Listed and Designated Events">Ofcom Code on Sports and Other Listed and Designated Events</a>. 2004 marked the first year that <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital television</a> and <a href="/wiki/Webcast" title="Webcast">webcasts</a> were used to cover an Olympic Games. The digital television service allowed up to five streamed channels covering the games, allowing more extensive coverage of minor sports, whilst the BBC's website permitted UK <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a> users to view live streams from a variety of events, and other countries to view delayed highlights. Live broadcasts were run throughout the day, with a highlights program on BBC1 following the close of the day's events.</p>
<p>The BBC's coverage was anchored (at various times of the day) by <a href="/wiki/Craig_Doyle" title="Craig Doyle">Craig Doyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clare_Balding" title="Clare Balding">Clare Balding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suzi_Perry" title="Suzi Perry">Suzi Perry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sue_Barker" title="Sue Barker">Sue Barker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rider" title="Steve Rider">Steve Rider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hazel_Irvine" title="Hazel Irvine">Hazel Irvine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Cram" title="Steve Cram">Steve Cram</a>. Expert analysts and commentators included <a href="/wiki/Sharron_Davies" title="Sharron Davies">Sharron Davies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jonathan_Edwards_(athlete)" title="Jonathan Edwards (athlete)">Jonathan Edwards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sally_Gunnell" title="Sally Gunnell">Sally Gunnell</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Johnson_(athlete)" title="Michael Johnson (athlete)">Michael Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Jackson" title="Colin Jackson">Colin Jackson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Redgrave" title="Steve Redgrave">Steve Redgrave</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eurosport" title="Eurosport">Eurosport</a> also ran coverage of the Games viewable in the UK – in accordance with the ITC Code, it can show live events, provided that such events can also be broadcast by the BBC (although the BBC can choose not to do so).</p>
<p>Radio coverage was provided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Five_Live" title="BBC Radio Five Live">BBC Radio Five Live</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_Radio_News" title="Independent Radio News">IRN</a>, and the events were also covered by the sports pages of the major newspapers.</p>
